# **KS0536 KS0537 Keyestudio Ultimate Starter Kit for Arduino**

[![ks0536](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/9201f8a8313d7e5912f625491c8b8287.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/9201f8a8313d7e5912f625491c8b8287.jpeg)

**1.Introduction**

Do you want to learn about programming?

As long as you are passionate about science and dare to explore new things, this kit is surely the best choice for you.

The kit is a learning kit for two programming methods, including Scratch graphical programming and C language programming based on Arduino. you can create numerous fascinating experiments with the PLUS mainboard，sensors，modules and electronic components.

As many as 35 project tutorials are provided, which contain detailed wiring diagrams, component knowledge, test code, and so on.

In addition, you can master the use of electronics, physics, science and programming by building up experiment with this kit.

1.  **Kit List**

**(KS0536 includes Plus mainboard, KS0537 does not include Plus mainboard.)**

| Resistance Card\*1 | Jumper Wire\*30 | M-F Dupont Wire\*20 | F-F Dupont Wire\*40 |  |

**3\. Keyestudio PLUS Motherboard**

The Keyestudio PLUS motherboard, fully compatible with the Arduino IDE control board, which is the core of this kit

It incorporates all functions of Arduino UNO R3. Additionally, more improvements on the PLUS board makes it powerful.

It is your best choice to build up circuits and programme.

**[![KS0486-VS](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/ad857bf77d618927b0b19a4e4f506dd5.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/ad857bf77d618927b0b19a4e4f506dd5.jpeg)**

**Specifications:**

-   Microcontroller: ATMEGA328P-AU
    
-   USB to serial chip: CP2102
    
-   Working voltage: DC 5V or 3.3V (DIP switch control)
    
-   External power supply: DC 6V to 15V (9V is recommended.)
    
-   Digital I/O pins: 14 (D0 to D13)
    
-   PWM channel: 6 (D3 D5 D6 D9 D10 D11)
    
-   Analog input channel (ADC): 8 (A0 to A7)
    
-   Each I/O port of DC output capacity: 20 mA
    
-   Output capacity of 3.3V port: 50 mA
    
-   Flash Memory: 32 KB（of which the bootloader uses 0.5 KB）
    
-   SRAM: 2 KB (ATMEGA328P-AU)
    
-   EEPROM:1 KB (ATMEGA328P-AU)
    
-   Clock speed: 16MHz
    
-   On-board LED pin: D13
    

**Pinout**

[![KS0486-sm](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/f75b95aa9c5d83bfc2f77143d8740ce4.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/f75b95aa9c5d83bfc2f77143d8740ce4.jpeg)

**Specialized Functions of Pins:**

-   Serial communication interface: D0 is RX, D1 is TX
    
-   PWM interface (pulse width modulation): D3 D5 D6 D9 D10 D11
    
-   External interrupt interface: D2(interrupt 0) and D3 (interrupt 1)
    
-   SPI communication interface: D10 is SS, D11 is MOSI, D12 is MISO, D13 is SCK
    
-   IIC communication port: A4 is SDA, A5 is SCL
    

**Note: The all experiments of this learning kit, the DIP switch on the Keyestudio PLUS control board is turned to the 5V terminal by default.**

**4.How to Download Arduino, Drivers and Library Files**

**1\. Install Windows Drivers**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/6cf6312dc7c7db27794b54d58a8bf80c.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/6cf6312dc7c7db27794b54d58a8bf80c.png)

1.1 Download and install Arduino software

Enter the Arduino official website: [https://www.arduino.cc/](https://www.arduino.cc/) and click "SOFTWARE" to enter the download page, as shown in the following figure.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/bfe8c9e405c71123dee7921eddff86d3.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/bfe8c9e405c71123dee7921eddff86d3.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/7250961db41ba42e4b881d77bd76a319.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/7250961db41ba42e4b881d77bd76a319.png) Then, select and download the corresponding installer according to your operating system. If you are a Windows user, please select "Windows Installer" to download the correct installation driver.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/894116c5cf0023dd9720946cfb441790.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/894116c5cf0023dd9720946cfb441790.png)

Click **Windows Win7 and newer** to download the installer for Arduino 1.8.16, which needs to be installed manually. And when clicking on the **Windows ZIP file**, the zip file of the Arduino 1.8.16 will be downloaded directly, and you only need to unzip it to complete the installation.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a983a2f2eceb968afbff8ba0f0376240.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a983a2f2eceb968afbff8ba0f0376240.png)

Generally, you can download it by clicking **JUST DOWNLOAD**. Of course, if you like, you can choose a small sponsorship to help the great Arduino open source.

(3) Once the Arduino software is downloaded, continue to install. When you receive **a warning from your operating system, allow the driver to install.** Click on **I Agree**, select the components you want to install and then click **Next**.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/00e334d3c756a2495da6f0d1b2db680a.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/00e334d3c756a2495da6f0d1b2db680a.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/de541d90a1cda992ad8e3f0cbaf95f94.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/de541d90a1cda992ad8e3f0cbaf95f94.png)

1.  Select the installation directory (The default directory is recommended.), then click **Install**.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/7da9aca1e8432c59372e7c7ab2574bd9.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/7da9aca1e8432c59372e7c7ab2574bd9.png)

1.  If the following interface appears, you should select **Install**.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/85b29de2aa791ecc77280ccde91e53c5.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/85b29de2aa791ecc77280ccde91e53c5.png)

This process will extract and install all the necessary files to properly execute the Arduino software (IDE).

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/739c41701fbcab202f0e587f534bad30.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/739c41701fbcab202f0e587f534bad30.png)

After the installation is complete, an Arduino software shortcut will be created on the desktop.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/d28223c55a30f949760779720fe4ec24.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/d28223c55a30f949760779720fe4ec24.png)

1.2 Install the drivers on the Windows system

**(Note: If the computer has already installed the drivers, you do not need to install the drivers again. If not, you need to do the following.)**

Drivers must be installed before using the Plus mainboard, otherwise the Plus mainboard will not be able to communicate with the computer. Unlike the USB series chip (ATMEGA8U2) of the Arduino UNO R3, the Plus mainboard uses the USB series CP2102 chip and the USB type-C interface. The CP2102 chip driver is included in Arduino IDE 1.8.0 and higher. Usually, you connect the Plus mainboard to the computer via a USB cable, the computer will recognize the hardware, and the WINDOWS system will automatically install the CP2102 driver. After a while, the CP2102 driver will be installed successfully.

**Note:**

1.  Please make sure your IDE is updated to version 1.8.0 or a later version.
    
2.  If the version of the Arduino IDE you downloaded is lower than 1.8.0, please download the CP2102 driver and install it manually.
    

Link to download CP2102 driver: [**https://fs.keyestudio.com/CP2102-WIN**](https://fs.keyestudio.com/CP2102-WIN)

If the driver installation fails, you need to install the driver manually.Please open the device manager of your computer, right-click "Computer" -----“Properties”-----“Device Manager”. Under Ports (COM &LPT) or Other devices, the yellow exclamation mark means CP2102 driver installation failed.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/9af2e34bf9bdd6675bdf5fa8cd291971.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/9af2e34bf9bdd6675bdf5fa8cd291971.png)

It shows that the driver of CP2102 has not been installed successfully, there will be a yellow exclamation mark. Double-click [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a2455b26773cb8d6cb3fccc605ea4dd7.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a2455b26773cb8d6cb3fccc605ea4dd7.png) and then click“**Update drive...**”to update driver.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a122cd6fef74eb5c0c7fe16fac2fed59.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a122cd6fef74eb5c0c7fe16fac2fed59.png)

Click“**Browse my computer for drivers**”to find the Arduino software we installed or downloaded.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a02d3e643231cfe267d4debf0ef258c4.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a02d3e643231cfe267d4debf0ef258c4.png)

There is a drives folder in the Arduino folder（[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/aae89b3213589edf1c320d5502489820.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/aae89b3213589edf1c320d5502489820.png)），open the drivers folder and you can see the drivers of CP210X series chips.

Click on“**Browse...**”, select the drivers of CP210X series chips and click“**Next**”.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/eb6ca318005b5c570ad4fbef73024351.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/eb6ca318005b5c570ad4fbef73024351.png)

After a while, the drivers are installed successfully.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/4f2af46602a5ef73985914170911c519.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/4f2af46602a5ef73985914170911c519.png)

Open the device manager, we will find the yellow exclamation mark disappeared. The driver of CP2102 is installed successfully.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/af2324b73308f1796b8b7c9dc14878e7.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/af2324b73308f1796b8b7c9dc14878e7.png)

1.3 Arduino IDE setting

Once the driver is successfully installed, the next step is to configure the Arduino IDE devices and ports. For the PLUS motherboard, click **Tools**→**Board** and select **Arduino Uno** (as shown in the figure below).

[![Untitled](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a7febd32a34ce315a54c84474773cd5f.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a7febd32a34ce315a54c84474773cd5f.png)

Then select the correct COM port. After the driver is successfully installed, you can see the corresponding COM port.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/af2324b73308f1796b8b7c9dc14878e7.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/af2324b73308f1796b8b7c9dc14878e7.png)

Click on **Tools**→**Port→COM3**

[![Untitled](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e26bb9d41470c0483c9e3d3c88827cc1.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e26bb9d41470c0483c9e3d3c88827cc1.png)

Before uploading the code program to the control board, let’s demonstrate the functions of each symbol in the Arduino IDE toolbar.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a62ae27ea21104076335994547e7f4e4.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a62ae27ea21104076335994547e7f4e4.png)

A - Used to verify whether there is any compiling mistakes or not.

B - Used to upload the program to your Arduino control board.

C - Used to create shortcut of a new sketch.

D - Used to directly open an example sketch.

E - Used to save the sketches.

F - Used to receive serial data from the board and send the serial data to the board's serial monitor.

1.4 Start first program

Open“**File**”to select“**Examples**”, and choose“**Blink**”from“**Basics**”，as shown below.

[![Untitled](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/7c41632de952712b23ae151a8fbdd4fd.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/7c41632de952712b23ae151a8fbdd4fd.png)

When the sketch (Blink) window opens, you can see the entire program in the window.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/38b6fe97f113b87344b56376c4472acd.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/38b6fe97f113b87344b56376c4472acd.png)

Set the board type and COM port, the corresponding board types and COM ports are shown in the lower right corner of the IDE.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/ec47a4eb583f7f620c07ee6df72dbc9e.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/ec47a4eb583f7f620c07ee6df72dbc9e.png)

Click [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/ddd21c81338ae1f6b7f84de2a3caecf0.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/ddd21c81338ae1f6b7f84de2a3caecf0.png) to start compiling the program and check errors.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/42409c71f2addaf018e231113c21b66e.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/42409c71f2addaf018e231113c21b66e.png)

Click [![IMG_275](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/9c9158a5d49baa740ea2f0048f655017.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/9c9158a5d49baa740ea2f0048f655017.png) to upload the program. After a few seconds, uploaded successfully.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/61449e463427bf8925a36e56c8e88b2f.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/61449e463427bf8925a36e56c8e88b2f.png)

The uploading is done. Using USB cable to power on, the on-board LEDs on the PLUS motherboard light up for 1 second and go off for 1 second, and the cycle continues. Congratulation, you finish the first program.

**2\. Install the Drivers on the MAC System**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a6fc83596009c574d8e29ef383748549.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a6fc83596009c574d8e29ef383748549.png)

2.1 Download and install Arduino software

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/5d58d3cf67b308423ddb9f286f6cb697.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/5d58d3cf67b308423ddb9f286f6cb697.png)

2.2 Download the drivers of CP2102

Link:

[https://wiki.keyestudio.com/How\_to\_Install\_the\_Driver\_of\_CP2102\_on\_MAC\_System](https://wiki.keyestudio.com/How_to_Install_the_Driver_of_CP2102_on_MAC_System)

**2.3 How to install the driver of CP2102**

**(Note: If the driver is already installed, just skip the following instruction)**

(1) Connect the PLUS mainboard to your MacOS computer with a USB cable, and open the Arduino IDE.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a72fe5a29c6af0cd24aba7ab59b4996e.emf)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a72fe5a29c6af0cd24aba7ab59b4996e.emf)

Click **Tools**→**Board:Arduino Uno** and **/dev/cu.usbserial-0001**.

[![IMG_257](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/37689ea487b506d66f8ee82a8e1418b9.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/37689ea487b506d66f8ee82a8e1418b9.png)

Click [![IMG_275](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/9c9158a5d49baa740ea2f0048f655017.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/9c9158a5d49baa740ea2f0048f655017.png) to upload the code. If the upload is successful, as shown in the figure below, it will show that the upload is successful.

[![IMG_258](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/4c804ad604a9fc682d5c472387039dfc.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/4c804ad604a9fc682d5c472387039dfc.png)

**Note: If the code program is uploaded successfully, you do not need to install the driver again, you can skip the following steps to install the driver. If not, you need to follow the steps below to install the CP2102 driver. Execute the following steps (2) to (13).**

(2) CP2102 drivers download link.

[https://www.silabs.com/products/development-tools/software/usb-to-uart-bridge-vcp-drivers](https://www.silabs.com/products/development-tools/software/usb-to-uart-bridge-vcp-drivers)

(3) Click to download the MacOS version.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/c09e7c279a858574756d1192b3a995aa.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/c09e7c279a858574756d1192b3a995aa.png)

(4) Unzip the downloaded package.

[![{6870A714-DDD1-1015-DC43-B1D5743E0666}](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/6870a714ddd11015dc43b1d5743e0666.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/6870a714ddd11015dc43b1d5743e0666.jpeg)

(5) Open the folder and double-click“**SiLabsUSBDriverDisk.dmg**”file.

[![IMG_261](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/61ae3e706a1c4afa7948d5fb2e797a6d.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/61ae3e706a1c4afa7948d5fb2e797a6d.png)

You can see the following files.

1.  Double-click\*\*“Install CP210x VCP Driver”,\*\* tick“**Don’t warn me when opening application on this disk image**”and click“**Open**”.

[![IMG_263](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/14f6ebb088e654abc2f0149645e34ed1.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/14f6ebb088e654abc2f0149645e34ed1.png)

[![{E3881FC6-7F40-B173-AA22-2A2A8A36ECAB}](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/b1cb125dccf6470ebe255f8f65b902eb.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/b1cb125dccf6470ebe255f8f65b902eb.jpeg)

1.  Click on“**Agree**”and select“**Continue**”.

[![{5D5929F6-B53A-0C03-7919-49AA20E7738D}](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/865dcc76cb7f58854b56f1020233f05e.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/865dcc76cb7f58854b56f1020233f05e.jpeg)

(9) Continue to click“**Continue**”, then enter your user password.

[![{15F1B01F-B066-9615-0B44-D5039DF02484}](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/1ef6d65b61ad7c6e0a3989ba59de74d5.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/1ef6d65b61ad7c6e0a3989ba59de74d5.jpeg)

[![{7B313247-7D6D-C1AD-1403-5E14567A2208}](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/cb6be428257143635fc4f729487549c5.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/cb6be428257143635fc4f729487549c5.jpeg)

**3\. Install Library Files to Arduino**

What are Libraries ?

Libraries are a collection of code that makes it easy for you to connect to a sensor, display, module, etc. For example, the built-in LiquidCrystal library help to talk to LCD displays. There are hundreds of additional libraries available on the Internet for download. Please refer to this website ([https://www.arduino.cc/en/Reference/Libraries](https://www.arduino.cc/en/Reference/Libraries)). The built-in libraries and some of the additional libraries are listed in.

How to Install a Library ?

**3.1 Manual installation**

(Windows system is taken as an example, MacOS can be used as a reference.)

When you want to add a library manually, you first have to exit the Arduino application, then you need to download the library as a ZIP file, decompress it and put it in the appropriate directory.

As an example, to download and install the IR Remote library, we go to the link: [https://github.com/shirriff/Arduino-IRremote](https://github.com/shirriff/Arduino-IRremote). Find the IR Remote library on GitHub. Download the IR Remote ZIP library by clicking the green “Code” button and then click “download ZIP”.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/bb6556490a4d698496daa663fb73dca2.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/bb6556490a4d698496daa663fb73dca2.png)

After downloading, unzip the IRremote library file package.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/888062840a4315aa5786890a6a580744.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/888062840a4315aa5786890a6a580744.png)

Then move the IRremote library file package to the Arduino folder.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/346d3a1d775659c11ec8711220e5702e.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/346d3a1d775659c11ec8711220e5702e.png)

Open the libraries folder in the Arduino folder and drag the Arduino- irremote -master folder into the Libraries folder.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/b9ddb20f044a39b304fffed86213908c.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/b9ddb20f044a39b304fffed86213908c.png)

In this way, the manual installation of the library file is completed.

Note: use the library files we provide, save you the trouble of downloading them.

Using the library files we provide, unzip each library file in turn, then copy and paste them into the libraries folder in the Arduino folder.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/201ce3acf9adf2bfb5132ac54ed76311.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/201ce3acf9adf2bfb5132ac54ed76311.png)

e.g.: Take [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a9ed380289a225adc9d8f7f25199ba90.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a9ed380289a225adc9d8f7f25199ba90.png) as an example. Click [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a9ed380289a225adc9d8f7f25199ba90.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a9ed380289a225adc9d8f7f25199ba90.png) to decompress it. Copy and paste the decompressed file package [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/aeaef0e27d77db862d4ac210285bcfa4.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/aeaef0e27d77db862d4ac210285bcfa4.png) into the libraries folder in the Arduino folder.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a506bdf07083606eec6a998bc359aeb8.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a506bdf07083606eec6a998bc359aeb8.png)

By analogy, use the above method to decompress the remaining library files, then copy and paste them into the libraries folder in the Arduino folder.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/36f2aba3c4b097856acb58332811f546.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/36f2aba3c4b097856acb58332811f546.png)

In this way, the library files are manually added.

## 5.Projects

## Project 1: Hello World

1.  **Introduction**

For Arduino beginners, we will start with some simple things. In this project, you only need a PLUS mainboard and a USB cable to complete the "Hello World!" project.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/640cb2f352765c54f899be8e494dfa6f.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/640cb2f352765c54f899be8e494dfa6f.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |
| --- | --- |
| Keyestudio PLUS Mainboard\*1 | USB Cable\*1 |

1.  **Connection**

**[![KS0486-sy2](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/b019e38e3fb807abc426eb30ddbd8884.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/b019e38e3fb807abc426eb30ddbd8884.jpeg)**

1.  **Code**

Arduino uses a serial monitor to display information such as print statements and sensor data. This is a very powerful tool for debugging long code. Let's first learn the“if”statement, which is a control structure in Arduino programming.

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 1

Hello World

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

char val;// defines variable "val"

void setup()

{

Serial.begin(9600);// sets baudrate to 9600

}

void loop()

{

if (Serial.available() > 0) {

val=Serial.read();// reads symbols assigns to "val"

if(val=='R')// checks input for the letter "R"

{ // if so,

Serial.println("Hello World!");// shows “Hello World !”.

}

}

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Select the correct Arduino IDE mainboard type and COM port, and click the **button**[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/0f40d5ce9a863c5de0caa6a80434643a.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/0f40d5ce9a863c5de0caa6a80434643a.png) on the Arduino IDE to upload the code. After successfully uploading, click the icon[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/2f6bca56f724e45a855335cb53ae9b4e.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/2f6bca56f724e45a855335cb53ae9b4e.png)to enter the serial display.

[![IMG_256](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/2fa344eb4c3715a1b3f05d1c3151ba24.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/2fa344eb4c3715a1b3f05d1c3151ba24.png)

Whenever you enter an "R" in the text box and click "Send", the serial monitor will display "Hello World!”.

## [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/cb3985773d77fd88f09db9296ce40987.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/cb3985773d77fd88f09db9296ce40987.png)

**Project 2: LED Blinking**

1.  **Introduction**

In this project, we will show you the LED flashing effect through Arduino's digital pins.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/1ba4075b92cfdc6c187aed3cbdcbd965.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/1ba4075b92cfdc6c187aed3cbdcbd965.png) | [![红 (4)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/7eb361d680dfa351f07f8527aeb37abd.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/7eb361d680dfa351f07f8527aeb37abd.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Keyestudio PLUS Mainboard\*1 | Red LED\*1 | 220Ω Resistor\*1 | Breadboard\*1 | Jumper Wire\*2 | USB Cable\*1 |

1.  **Component Knowledge**
    
2.  **LED:**
    

**[![KS0306](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/081141eed6146deed2bfbd8e55a8465b.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/081141eed6146deed2bfbd8e55a8465b.jpeg)**

It is a kind of semiconductor called "light-emitting diode", which is an electronic device made of semiconductor materials (silicon, selenium, germanium, etc.). It has an anode and a cathode. The short lead (cathode) is grounded. The long lead (anode)is connected to 5V.

[![red-led-pinout-schematic](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/f70404aa49540fd7aecae944c7c01f83.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/f70404aa49540fd7aecae944c7c01f83.jpeg)

1.  **Resistor**

A resistor is an electronic component in a circuit that restricts or regulates the flow current flow. Its unit is(Ω). 1 mΩ= 1000 kΩ，1kΩ= 1000Ω.

!\[QMLZB\[EZHQ}ITP[9@7VR}LA](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/8a86f65cf820d08e8956daa70d1c4195.jpeg) [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/f6079fe22518f0fc1b0c3a3b93a516a1.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/f6079fe22518f0fc1b0c3a3b93a516a1.png)

We can use resistors to protect sensitive components, such as LEDs. The strength of the resistance is marked on the body of the resistor with an electronic color code. Each color code represents a number, and you can refer to it in a resistance card.

\-Color 1 – 1st Digit

\-Color 2 – 2nd Digit

\-Color 3 – 3rd Digit

\-Color 4 – Multiplier

\-Color 5 – Tolerance

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/c3df005312cd9f6d4cdae6abf3cddb83.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/c3df005312cd9f6d4cdae6abf3cddb83.png)

In this kit, we provide eight 5-band resistors with different resistance values. Take three 5-band resistors as an example.

220Ω resistor\*10

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)

10KΩ resistor\*10

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/246cf3885dc837c458a28123885c9f7b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/246cf3885dc837c458a28123885c9f7b.png)

1KΩ resistor\*10

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/19f5dfc51adfd79b04c3b164529767ed.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/19f5dfc51adfd79b04c3b164529767ed.png)

The connection between current, voltage, and resistance can be expressed by the formula: I=U/R.In the figure below, if the voltage is 3V, the current through R1 is: I = U / R = 3 V / 10 KΩ= 0.0003A= 0.3mA.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/b3eec552e4dfad361833730698621776.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/b3eec552e4dfad361833730698621776.png)

**（3）Breadboard**

A breadboard is used to build and test circuits quickly before finalizing any circuit design. The breadboard has many holes into which circuit components like integrated circuits and resistors can be inserted. A typical breadboard is as follows.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/612c1381811b2d780d5f6ed6a7ec3701.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/612c1381811b2d780d5f6ed6a7ec3701.png)

The bread board has strips of metal which run underneath the board and connect the holes on the top of the board. The metal strips are laid out as shown below. Note that the top and bottom rows of holes are connected horizontally while the remaining holes are connected vertically.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/b45e70b961537035c85878b73d371725.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/b45e70b961537035c85878b73d371725.png)

The first two rows (top) and the last two rows (bottom) of the breadboard are used for the positive (+) and negative (-) terminals of the power supply, respectively. The conductive layout of the breadboard is shown in the following diagram.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/d5478bd5eac558252cbc235479d979eb.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/d5478bd5eac558252cbc235479d979eb.png)

When we connect DIP (Dual In-line Packages) components, such as integrated circuits, microcontrollers, chips and so on, we can see that a groove in the middle isolates the middle part, so the top and bottom of the groove is not connected. DIP components can be connected as shown in the figure below.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/50caf14e911c4244779e99445c658db6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/50caf14e911c4244779e99445c658db6.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/9b66ae2199e77fbc99b7b278dac0b567.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/9b66ae2199e77fbc99b7b278dac0b567.png)

1.  **Circuit Diagram and Wiring Diagram**

As shown in the diagram, we use digital pin 10 and connect one LED to a 220 ohm resistor to avoid high current to damage the LED.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/d02bdc6699a72aa840e4b749fef2b477.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/d02bdc6699a72aa840e4b749fef2b477.png)

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 2

LED\_Blinking

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int ledPin = 10; // defines numeric pin 10.

void setup()

{

pinMode(ledPin, OUTPUT);// defines PIN with connected LED as output

}

void loop()

{

digitalWrite(ledPin, HIGH); // turn on LED

delay(1000); // wait a second.

digitalWrite(ledPin, LOW); // turn off LED

delay(1000); // wait a second

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Upload the project code, wire up components according to the wiring diagram, and power on. The LED will blink.

1.  **Explanation**

**pinMode(ledPin，OUTPUT)**: Before using the Arduino's pins, you need to tell the control board whether it is INPUT or OUTPUT. We use a built-in function “pinMode()” to do this.

**digitalWrite(ledPin，HIGH)** : When using a pin as an OUTPUT, it can be commanded as HIGH (output 5V) or LOW (output 0V).

**Project 3: Breathing Led**

1.  **Introduction**

In this project, we will learn the PWM control of ARDUINO. PWM is Pulse Width Modulation, which is a technique that encodes analog signal levels into digital signal levels. We will use PWM to control the brightness of LED.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/1ba4075b92cfdc6c187aed3cbdcbd965.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/1ba4075b92cfdc6c187aed3cbdcbd965.png) | [![红 (4)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/3ec5906fad2172708d449390140f55e6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/3ec5906fad2172708d449390140f55e6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Keyestudio Plus Mainboard\*1 | Red LED\*1 | 220Ω Resistor\*1 | Breadboard\*1 | Jumper Wire\*2 | USB Cable\*1 |

1.  **Component Knowledge**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/6549bdbfd4e7b6b2b341012105d655e8.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/6549bdbfd4e7b6b2b341012105d655e8.png)

**Working principle:** It can control the brightness of LED, the speed of DC motors and Servo motors, and outputs square wave signal. If we want to dim the LED, we can change the ON(open) and OFF(close) time of the signal. When we change the time of ON and OFF fast enough, then the brightness of the LED will change. Here are some terms related to PWM as follows.

ON (open)：When the signal is high.

OFF (close)：When the signal is low.

Period: It is the sum of the time of On and Off.

Duty cycle: The percentage of time when the signal is at a high level for a certain period of time. At 50% duty cycle and 1Hz frequency, the LED will be on for half a second and off for the other half of a second.

[![IMG_256](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a439e1bd8a4578b43b7188c821d58594.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a439e1bd8a4578b43b7188c821d58594.jpeg)

**Arduino and PWM**

The Arduino IDE has a built-in function “analogWrite()” that can be used to generate PWM signals. Most of the pins generate signals with a frequency of about 490Hz and we can use this function to give values from 0 to 255.

“analogWrite(0)” indicates a signal with 0% duty cycle. “analogWrite(127)” indicates a signal with 50% duty cycle. “analogWrite(255)” indicates a signal with 100% duty cycle. On the Plus control board, the PWM pins are 3, 5, 6, 9, 10, and 11. PWM pins are marked with the “~”symbol. In this project, you will learn how to get the PWM output from the digital pins of the Plus control board and control the brightness of the LED by code.

**4\. Circuit Diagram and Wiring Diagram**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/170100d0209991de69f53fac71db8d9f.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/170100d0209991de69f53fac71db8d9f.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/7a47b49003db03eec77200d847e6d61c.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/7a47b49003db03eec77200d847e6d61c.png)

**Note:**

How to connect the LED

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/42ff6f405dfa128593827de5aa03e94b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/42ff6f405dfa128593827de5aa03e94b.png)

How to identify the 220Ω 5-band resistor

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)

**5\. Code**

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 3

Breathing\_Led

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int ledPin = 6;

void setup()

{

pinMode(ledPin,OUTPUT);

}

void loop(){

for (int value = 0 ; value < 255; value=value+1){

analogWrite(ledPin, value);

delay(5);

}

for (int value = 255; value >0; value=value-1){

analogWrite(ledPin, value);

delay(5);

} }

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

After burning the project code, connecting the wires according to the wiring diagram, and powering on, the LED lights up gradually, and then gradually darkens.

1.  **Explanation**

When we need to execute a sentence repeatedly, we can use the “for” statement.

The “for”statement format is as follows:

[![图1(1)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/65da124bdd0ea488291c71c6b879fe95.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/65da124bdd0ea488291c71c6b879fe95.jpeg)

The loop sequence of“for”statement is as follows:

Round 1: 1 → 2 → 3 → 4

Round 2: 2 → 3 → 4

…

Until 2 does not hold and the “for” statement loop ends.

Knowing this sequence, go back to the code.

**for (int value = 0; value < 255; value=value+1){**

**...}**

**for (int value = 255; value >0; value=value-1){**

**...}**

These two for statements, which realize that the value can continuously increases from 0 to 255, then decreases from 255 to 0. The loop continues indefinitely.

In the “for”statement, involving a new function “analogWrite()”.

We know that the digital port has only two states, 0 and 1. How to send an analog value to a digital pin? This function will be used. Take a look at the Arduino board and look at the digital pins. You will find that 6 of the pins are marked with "~". These pins are different from other pins in that they can output PWM signals.

The format as follow:

**analogWrite(pin,value)**

The “analogWrite()” function is used to input an analog value from 0 to 255 to the PWM port. Therefore, the value is between 0 and 255. Note that the “analogWrite()” function can only write to the digital pins with PWM function, that is, the 3, 5, 6, 9, 10, and 11 pins.

## Project 4: Traffic Light

1.  **Introduction**

Traffic lights are closely related to people's daily lives. Traffic lights generally show red, yellow, and green. Everyone should obey the traffic rules, which can avoid many traffic accidents. In this project, we will use a PLUS board and some LEDs (red, green and yellow) to simulate the traffic lights.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![KS0486-1](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/5d8009d7d980c89a24adf1e186afa94f.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/5d8009d7d980c89a24adf1e186afa94f.jpeg) | [![红 (4)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/afa6edd3ff90b027a6f43995a6fb15a2.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/afa6edd3ff90b027a6f43995a6fb15a2.png) | [![y](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/0c1b0f91b4e56bcbc235d06b48809ac9.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/0c1b0f91b4e56bcbc235d06b48809ac9.png) | [![绿 (5)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/6c688493b558ed5f3e90e7dab38cbd93.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/6c688493b558ed5f3e90e7dab38cbd93.png) |

How to connect an LED

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/42ff6f405dfa128593827de5aa03e94b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/42ff6f405dfa128593827de5aa03e94b.png)

How to identify the 220Ω 5-band resistor

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)

1.  **Code**

The flashing time of each LED should be the same as the traffic lights. In this program, we use “Arduino delay ()” to control the delay time.

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 4

Traffic\_Light

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int redled =10; // initializes digital PIN 10

int yellowled =7; // initializes digital PIN 7

int greenled =4; // initializes digital PIN 4

void setup()

{

pinMode(redled, OUTPUT);// sets digital PIN 10 to “output”

pinMode(yellowled, OUTPUT); // sets digital PIN 7 to “output”

pinMode(greenled, OUTPUT); // sets digital PIN 4 to “output”

}

void loop()

{

digitalWrite(greenled, HIGH);// turns on LED

delay(5000);// delays 5 seconds

digitalWrite(greenled, LOW); // turns off LED

for(int i=0;i<3;i++)// flashes 3 times.

{

delay(500);// delays 0.5 second

digitalWrite(yellowled, HIGH);// turns on LED

delay(500);// delays 0.5 second

digitalWrite(yellowled, LOW);// turns off LED

}

delay(500);// delays 0.5 second

digitalWrite(redled, HIGH);// turns on LED

delay(5000);// delays 5 second

digitalWrite(redled, LOW);// turns off LED

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Upload the code and power on, the green LED will light up for 5s then go off. Next, the yellow one will blink for 3 times and red LED will be on for 5s then go off.

**Project 5: RGB LED**

**1\. Introduction**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/94bdff69e438989d8e0934e57f2e5c00.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/94bdff69e438989d8e0934e57f2e5c00.png)

In this project, we will introduce the RGB LED and show you how to use the Plus control board to control the RGB LED. Even though RGB LED is very basic, it is also a great way to learn the fundamentals of electronics and coding.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![KS0486-1](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/0fb8e2f3134f1770374ff0508075840a.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/0fb8e2f3134f1770374ff0508075840a.jpeg) | [![图层 2 拷贝 2](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/f1a86fc81ab4b043263ce7e01e14d470.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/f1a86fc81ab4b043263ce7e01e14d470.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/098a2730d0b0a2a4b2079e0fc87fd38b.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |

**3\. Component Knowledge**

**RGB LED：**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/03a7f4cce9c57f7e38465eed7bb18688.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/03a7f4cce9c57f7e38465eed7bb18688.jpeg)

The monitors mostly adopt the RGB color standard, and all the colors on the computer screen are composed of the three colors of red, green and blue mixed in different proportions.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/5a0792145e8a7d9038bf9de389d75fc6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/5a0792145e8a7d9038bf9de389d75fc6.png)[![RGBColourModel](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/8bf1339719a922f2fbc1e01a4347b4ab.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/8bf1339719a922f2fbc1e01a4347b4ab.png)

This RGB LED has pin R, G and B and a common cathode. To change its brightness, we can use the PWM pins which can give different duty cycle signals to the RGB LED to produce different colors.

1.  **Circuit Diagram and Wiring Diagram**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/75f5c237603aac47402e452e5e6a3ce6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/75f5c237603aac47402e452e5e6a3ce6.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/846746ec683d91428ac6f9484b081952.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/846746ec683d91428ac6f9484b081952.png)

**Note:**

RGB LED longest pin (common cathode) connected to GND.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/1584356c63bf99934ae0810ee02dced3.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/1584356c63bf99934ae0810ee02dced3.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/55c0199544e9819328f6d5778f10d7d0.png)

1.  **Code**

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 starter learning kit

Project 5

RGB LED

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int redpin = 11; // select the pin for the red LED

int bluepin =9; // select the pin for the blue LED

int greenpin =10;// select the pin for the green LED

int val;

void setup() {

pinMode(redpin, OUTPUT);

pinMode(bluepin, OUTPUT);

pinMode(greenpin, OUTPUT);

}

void loop()

{

for(val=255; val>0; val--)

{

analogWrite(11, val);

analogWrite(10, 255-val);

analogWrite(9, 128-val);

delay(1);

}

for(val=0; val<255; val++)

{

analogWrite(11, val);

analogWrite(10, 255-val);

analogWrite(9, 128-val);

delay(1);

}

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Upload the project code, wire up, power up and wait a few seconds, you will see a colorful LED.

**Project 6: Flowing Light**

1.  **Introduction**

In our daily life, we can see many billboards made up of different colors of LED. They constantly change the light to attract the attention of customers. In this project, we will use Plus control board with 5 LEDs to achieve the effect of flowing water.

1.  **Components Required**

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 6

Flowing\_Light

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int BASE = 2 ;// I/O PIN for the first LED

int NUM = 5; // amount of LEDs

void setup()

{

for (int i = BASE; i < BASE + NUM; i ++)

{

pinMode(i, OUTPUT); // sets I/O PIN to "output"

}

}

void loop()

{

for (int i = BASE; i < BASE + NUM; i ++)

{

digitalWrite(i, LOW); //sets I/O PIN to "low", turns off LEDs one after the other

delay(200); // delay

}

for (int i = BASE; i < BASE + NUM; i ++)

{

digitalWrite(i, HIGH); // sets I/O PIN to "high", turns on LEDs one after the other

delay(200); // delay

}

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

After burning the project code, connecting the wires and powering on, the 5 LEDs connected to the D2 to D6 pins of the development board will gradually light up and then gradually go off.

**Project 7: Active Buzzer**

1.  **Introduction**

Active buzzer is a sound making element, widely used on computers, printers, alarms, electronic toys, telephones, timers, etc. It has an inner vibration source. In this project, we will use a PLUS control board to control the active buzzer to buzz.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![KS0486-1](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/ca7cf6e6d64e942d8c7a101a023e44fc.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/ca7cf6e6d64e942d8c7a101a023e44fc.jpeg) | !\[WV[4\_HQIMNH(NGS\`TGD8U3U](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/4b4f653a76a82a3b413855493cc58fba.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Keyestudio Plus Mainboard\*1 | Active Buzzer\*1 | Breadboard \*1 | Jumper Wires | USB Cable\*1 |

**3\. Component Knowledge**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/11ec5ddc982db9928341e858aab94652.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/11ec5ddc982db9928341e858aab94652.png)

The active buzzer inside has a simple oscillator circuit which can convert constant direct current into a certain frequency pulse signal. Once active buzzer receives a high level, it will sound. The passive buzzer is an integrated electronic buzzer with no internal vibration source. It must be driven by 2K to 5K square wave instead of a DC signal. The appearance of the two buzzers is very similar, but passive buzzers come with a green circuit board, and active buzzers come with a black tape. Passive buzzers don't have positive pole, but active buzzers have.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/0f9825969867ac2d65bb1a19ed0ad2ab.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/0f9825969867ac2d65bb1a19ed0ad2ab.png)

1.  **Circuit Diagram and Wiring Diagram**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/a33b2bcd705fdcc293948b4cbeb58ae2.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/a33b2bcd705fdcc293948b4cbeb58ae2.png)

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/1213ca87362f1b4a1443ba3138da4b8e.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/1213ca87362f1b4a1443ba3138da4b8e.png)

Note: The positive terminal ("+"/long pin) of the active buzzer is connected to pin 8, and the negative terminal (short pin) is connected to GND.

1.  **Code**

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

/\*

Keyestudio 2021 Starter Kit

Project 7

Active\_buzzer

http//[www.keyestudio.com](http://www.keyestudio.com/)

\*/

int buzzerPin = 8;

void setup ()

{

pinMode (buzzerPin, OUTPUT);

}

void loop ()

{

digitalWrite (buzzerPin, HIGH);

delay (500);

digitalWrite (buzzerPin, LOW);

delay (500);

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Upload the project code, wire up and power up, then the active buzzer buzzes.

**Project 8: Passive Buzzer**

1.  **Introduction**

In this project, we will learn the passive buzzer and use the Plus control board to control the passive buzzer to play a song. Unlike an active buzzer, a passive buzzer can emit sounds of different frequencies.

1.  **Components Required**

| [![KS0486-1](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/ca7cf6e6d64e942d8c7a101a023e44fc.jpeg)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/ca7cf6e6d64e942d8c7a101a023e44fc.jpeg) | !\[H4QG0GNSDN2S4\]TSS)6UP4J\](media/d1ea1bb2b2749820cab389d5b85b838b.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e380dd26e4825be9a768973802a55fe6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/e9a8d050105397bb183512fb4ffdd2f6.png) | [![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/755ba492c38e44d91e8b2c120dc64904.png) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Keyestudio Plus Mainboard\*1 | Passive Buzzer\*1 | Breadboard\*1 | Jumper Wires | USB Cable\*1 |

**3\. Component Knowledge**

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/8d0020e53824072cbe9d4f7d2f8acb4f.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/8d0020e53824072cbe9d4f7d2f8acb4f.png)

A passive buzzer is an integrated electronic buzzer with no internal vibration source. It must be driven by 2K to 5K square wave, not a DC signal. The two buzzers are very similar in appearance, but one buzzer with a green circuit board is a passive buzzer, while the other with black tape is an active buzzer. Passive buzzers cannot distinguish between positive polarity while active buzzers can.

[![](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/fc42c5ed014609ff0b290ee5361bb2fd.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/fc42c5ed014609ff0b290ee5361bb2fd.png)

#define NOTE\_CS6 1109

#define NOTE\_D6 1175

#define NOTE\_DS6 1245

#define NOTE\_E6 1319

#define NOTE\_F6 1397

#define NOTE\_FS6 1480

#define NOTE\_G6 1568

#define NOTE\_GS6 1661

#define NOTE\_A6 1760

#define NOTE\_AS6 1865

#define NOTE\_B6 1976

#define NOTE\_C7 2093

#define NOTE\_CS7 2217

#define NOTE\_D7 2349

#define NOTE\_DS7 2489

#define NOTE\_E7 2637

#define NOTE\_F7 2794

#define NOTE\_FS7 2960

#define NOTE\_G7 3136

#define NOTE\_GS7 3322

#define NOTE\_A7 3520

#define NOTE\_AS7 3729

#define NOTE\_B7 3951

#define NOTE\_C8 4186

#define NOTE\_CS8 4435

#define NOTE\_D8 4699

#define NOTE\_DS8 4978

#define REST 0

int tempo=114; // change this to make the song slower or faster

int buzzer = 8;// initializes digital I/O PIN to control the buzzer

// notes of the moledy followed by the duration

// a 4 means a quarter note, 8 an eighteenth , 16 sixteenth, so on

// !!negative numbers are used to represent dotted notes

// so -4 means a dotted quarter note, that is, a quarter plus an eighteenth

int melody\[\] = {

NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_G4,4,//1

NOTE\_G4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_D4,4,

NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,4,

NOTE\_E4,-4, NOTE\_D4,8, NOTE\_D4,2,

NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_G4,4,//4

NOTE\_G4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_D4,4,

NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,4,

NOTE\_D4,-4, NOTE\_C4,8, NOTE\_C4,2,

NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_C4,4,//8

NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,8, NOTE\_F4,8, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_C4,4,

NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,8, NOTE\_F4,8, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_D4,4,

NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_G3,2,

NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_G4,4,//12

NOTE\_G4,4, NOTE\_F4,4, NOTE\_E4,4, NOTE\_D4,4,

NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_C4,4, NOTE\_D4,4, NOTE\_E4,4,

NOTE\_D4,-4, NOTE\_C4,8, NOTE\_C4,2

};

// sizeof gives the number of bytes, each int value is composed of two bytes (16 bits)

// there are two values per note (pitch and duration), so for each note there are four bytes

int notes=sizeof(melody)/sizeof(melody\[0\])/2;

// this calculates the duration of a whole note in ms (60s/tempo)\*4 beats

int wholenote = (60000 \* 4) / tempo;

int divider = 0, noteDuration = 0;

void setup() {

// iterate over the notes of the melody

// remember, the array is twice the number of notes (notes + durations)

for (int thisNote = 0; thisNote < notes \* 2; thisNote = thisNote + 2) {

// calculates the duration of each note

divider = melody\[thisNote + 1\];

if (divider > 0) {

noteDuration = (wholenote) / divider; // regular note, just proceed

} else if (divider < 0) {

// dotted notes are represented with negative durations!!

noteDuration = (wholenote) / abs(divider);

noteDuration \*= 1.5; // increases the duration in half for dotted notes

}

// we only play the note for 90% of the duration, leaving 10% as a pause

tone(buzzer, melody\[thisNote\], noteDuration\*0.9);

// Wait for the specief duration before playing the next note

delay(noteDuration);

noTone(buzzer); // stop the waveform generation before the next note

}

}

void loop() {

// if you want to repeat the song forever,

// just paste the setup code here instead.

}

//\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*\*

1.  **Result**

Upload the project code, wire up and power on, then the passive buzzer will play a song.

**Project 9: 74HC595N Controls 7 LEDs**

1.  **Introduction**

For a PLUS mainboard, it has only 22 I/O ports, how do we light up a large number of LEDs? In this project, we will use 74HC595N to control 7 LEDs to save port resources.

1.  **Components Required**

(4)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/raw/master/media/3ec5906fad2172708d449390140f55e6.png)](https://github.com/keyestudio/KS0536-KS0537--Keyestudio-Ultimate-Starter-Kit-for-Arduino/blob/master/media/3ec5906fad2172708d449390140f55e6.png)
